
   Message Format
  ----------------

  Message #1 of 8173 <"- ASCII Signiture Rebuilt"|"- ASCII Signiture As-Is">*

  <Subject>

  <Date/Time>

  <Person & email address>

  <2 blank separator lines then...>

  <Message - "As-Is">

  <2 blank lines, then @'s as divider line between messages>


  * ASCII signitures have been rebuilt where possible.
    Unfortunately Yahoo store messages in a way which means more than 1 space
    is stored as just 1 space. Viewing the message source, and then trying to
    view HTML source in Firefox didn't make any difference.
    Where I have been unable to rebuild the ASCII signitures I have simply put
    "ASCII Signiture As-Is" by the message number.

    Thanks to Andrew Allen for preserving Peter Cahill's ASCII signiture for
    me (see message 1613) in November 1998.

    Thanks to Michael Cox, as I was able to cross-reference some emails from
    the Onelist archives with ones posted to the Yahoo one to reinstate email
    addresses that Yahoo has discarded, and rebuild some ASCII signitures.


   Message From Archivist
  ------------------------

   I hope everyone enjoys reading the messages and appreciates me archiving
   them. It took hours of work to get all the info into this file and then 
   rebuild the ASCII signitures as best as I could.
   Don't forget to join, or atleast visit, the Yahoo! AMOS-LIST group:

     http://groups.yahoo.com/group/amos-list


          - Andrew D. Burton, August 2007
            aliensrcooluk@yahoo.co.uk

On 01-Jul-98, Zangiacomi Sylvain wrote:
> 1) Where is the Amos web site ?

Which one?

> 5) Is there a possibility to loop voices or samples
> independantly ?

Try using a pattern with it.

Sam Loop On : Sam Loop Off %1010

That makes voices 2 and 4 loop, 1 and 3 not.

	Message #160 of 8173

Dir First$, Dir Next$

Wed Jul 1, 1998 11:33 pm
Rod Whiteley <rwhiteley@magnet.com.au>


Dear Amos-ers,
I'm having a problem with a programme which is using Dir First$ then Dir Next$
to scan folders for sequential text files for subsequent manipulation. The
problem is twofold;
Firstly, these commands append a space to the start of the filename and the
file size to the end of the name. This can be worked around easily enough, but
is there an alternative? I thought there may be a Config item, but have
searched to no avail.
Secondly, and more importantly, some files with very long names are truncated
by Dir Next$, so when you then use this command to open the files you'll get a
'File Not Found', e.g. if the file names were, say "An extremely long
filename_Seq", and "A shortie_Seq"
F$=Dir Next$
Rem: This will return F$ as " An extremely long filXX" Note the extra leading
space and the file size (XX) and " A Shortie XX"
P=Instr(F$,"_Seq") : Rem Find the end of the filename (and make sure it's one
that I'm after) So this will fail for the long filenames
F$ = Mid$(F$,2,P+2) : Rem Lose the leading space, and truncate to the end of
"_Seq"
Open In 1,F$
Doesn't work for long filenames, and retreats with a 'File Not Found'
Any ideas?
Rod

--
Mitchell & Whiteley Physiotherapy.

	Message #164 of 8173 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Dir First$, Dir Next$

Thu Jul 2, 1998 3:17 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org>


On 01-Jul-98, Rod Whiteley wrote:
>Firstly, these commands append a space to the start of the filename and the
>Secondly, and more importantly, some files with very long names are truncated

Annoying, but true. The best way around it is to use the GUI extension. Not
only will your prog be on the wb screen (or at least in intuition) it will use
the amiga file requesters. If you'd rather the program do it itself, try this:

Exec "Dir >RAM:temp YourDirHere"
Open In 1,"RAM:Temp"
<scan for filenames>
Close 1
Kill "RAM:Temp"

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark
                                  giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org
                           http://www.hicksville.dyn.ml.org/~giark/

	Message #165 of 8173 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Transp Anim's, Text Scrollies and Vu-Meters

Thu Jul 2, 1998 8:04 am
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 01-Jul-98, Phil Price wrote:

>Hello Amos Guru's,

Hi!

>Right I have more questions, Coz Of more things to add to my Music Disk :)
>Also thnx for all yourhelp on other points, I have found your the best list
>Out of all the ones in on :)

> o. I what a small (30x30 ish) Spinnig Logo, Or summint, My Screen Is a
>640x256 one but I what My logo to be normal (square) 320x256
>dimensions, Also , I what my 0 colour to be transp. :) How Do I go
>About doing this, I have not a clue, thnax .

Is your logo 30x30, or 320x256 ?!?
well, you can either have all frames saved as diffrent bobs or a Iffanim
or you can code up some asm routine to rotate it.

> o. How do I create a text scoller on some part of my screen , that Jut
> displayes, preset text, I woull like the font to be anything, exept
>Topaz. :/, prefebly my own font :)

Theres a example of how to do this some where an the prodictivity2 disk.

> o. How do I create a vu-meter, (Protraker and Old Octamed Style) in some
>coner of my screen ?!?

simple, VERY simple ;D
just use =Vumeter(chan), where chan is music channel 0-3.
then it will return how loud the current sample/tune is playing
in the channel, I think its a number between 1-64.
The just draw a box or something with the result of the vumeter added on.

I think that there is a few examples of this on Mushs site.

>wel thnx for all your help, I know this all seems like I'm adding Ponintless
>Eyecady , but It has to be done :) I have to keep the end usser interested
>in the Music, and kepping thier computeron :)

hehe

cya,

	Message #167 of 8173 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Transp Anim's, Text Scrollies and Vu-Meters

Sat Mar 7, 1998 9:58 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi All

> o. I what a small (30x30 ish) Spinnig Logo, Or summint, My Screen Is a
>640x256 one but I what My logo to be normal (square) 320x256
>dimensions, Also , I what my 0 colour to be transp. :) How Do I go
>About doing this, I have not a clue, thnax .

Do you mean like the tv logos in the top-right of the screen.

The best way of doing this is to use a sprite amal animation. The logo
will be lowres (so you'll have to change the anim) but it will be
lowres even on hires screens and it will be transparent and will
not affect changes on screen. The only problem is that it'll have to
have the right palette in colours 16-31.

I've sent an example of how that works.

The other questions have been answered by Peter Cahill, and I'm sure
if you look in PD libs you'll find good examples of both.


See ya.


--

	Message #179 of 8173 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: ext

Sat Jul 4, 1998 12:07 pm
Jens Vang Petersen <top_cat@post8.tele.dk>


Hello Hakan

On 04-Jul-98, Hakan Venderlof smashed the keyboard with:
> From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>
>
> Could someone send info
> about what extensions are good...
>

That sure depends on what you'd like to make, but if we take a look at
the 'free' ones, I'd say that 'EasyLife' and 'JD' is the ones that can
be of general use.. 'GUI' is usefull to support intuition and AGA, while
'tools' is great for 'advanced' use. 'Locale' is ofcourse some very
powerfull support of the locale.library, and 'DOOM' is the best music-
player around.. Among shareware/comercial extensions the 'AMCAF' will
always be usefull, OS_DevKit gives some very powerfull support of
the system (Intuition, AGA, locale, etc..), I don't think I have to
mention the compiler. LDos and LSerial is only availeble in a version
with a stupid error-requester (The author don't support amiga anymore),
but if you make sure you call the commands the right way then there's
no problems with that, LDos supports disc-commands and AREXX while
LSerial is the most powerfull access to the serial-port I've ever
seen.. The Craft extension can also be usefull, if you can find
it anywhere.. Finaly I most mention the Turbo+ V2.0 as a very powerfull
graphic-oriented extension, but the author don't appear to support
it anymore so either go for a 'illegal' version or get the old
freeware 'Turbo' extension...

All in all, extensions is a matter of personal taste, it depends
on what you like to program (games/demos/utilities), and how you
want things to work. I LOVE the OS_DevKit, becourse it gives
some direct access to the system and intuition, others prefer the
GUI for the same job becourse it's more 'idiot-proof'... I think
just about anyone on this list has some extension that he/she thinks
is the best becourse "- It's just what I need.."
--
A load of kind regards from

	Message #182 of 8173

Re: (no subject)

Sat Jul 4, 1998 5:27 pm
Bernie Noel <bnoel@club-internet.fr>


> 1) Where is the Amos web site ?

The official site is http://www.seta.it/amos/
It's called "The AMOS Factory".

> 2) Are there any extentions or patchs to save Bob Banks
> to FAST RAM ? and for Sample Banks, Music Banks.
> In fact, can we use FAST RAM for something when
> programming in Amos ?

For samples, the trick is to store them in a Data Bank in Fast RAM, and
reserve a much smaller Data Bank in Chip RAM, the size of the biggest sample.
When you want to play a sample, copy it from Fast RAM to Chip RAM (using Copy)
and then play it from the Chip Bank (using Sam Raw). It's very fast, and not
too complicated.
There is no 'realistic' solution for Bobs.

> 4) How can I test (if possible) multikey pression :
> for example I need to test if the keys 'a' and 'z' (and
> some others) are pressed together.

Use 'If Scancode() And Scancode() Then...'
But beware, the letters won't have the same scancode on a QWERTY and an AZERTY
keyboard...

Regards to all (et salut à toi!)

Bernie

* de Jong * <joopdejong@wxs.nl>


On 26-jun-98 Alastair Murray wrote:

>From: "Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>

>Firstly a suggestion to the people coding the new AMOS. Because of
>all the problems with AMOS now and again I get really annoyed with it
>and consider leaving it to code in something else. Knowing that a new
>version is being produced is very good for keeping me with it but
>when I don't hear anything about it I get a bit disillusioned again.
>How about giving us regular progress reports so we know how it is
>going and what it will be like?

>Secondly... bloody AMOS compiler.
>My program Backbone is getting quite large now and all of a sudden
>AMOS refuses to compile it (with or without GUI compiler). Usually it
>just stops dead 30% of the way through but on the rare occasion when
>it does compile it, the program doesn't work. Errors are also
>reported where there aren't any. Once it even wrote a 10MB file onto

If I renember correctly some years ago someone posted a list
of possible causes of problems with the compiler to the amoslist.
Try to find it in the archives on Aminet. Some things are:

- Large amount of data lines in the program
- Icon banks (uneven length??)
- Bug in amospro compiler. One line in the amospro compiler needs to
be changed in order to allow all extension slots to work with the compiler.

	Message #187 of 8173 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Argghh - Extensions

Sun Jul 5, 1998 10:50 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi All,

>Hello Amos'ers,

>'m getting rally anoyed with AmosPro, When I add xtensions
>(GUI,DoomMusic,AmCafe) None of them werk, Even though They are in the
>interpter Loaded Extensions when I look, :( This is really a problem, All
>then extension's Peograms say Exension [x] not loaded :( Is there any thing
>that can fix this, I have installed all the .lib files to APSysytem, All
>these problems have happedned after I Archived Amos, and split it into 800k
>files to stick onto disk before my HD For,,at (Chusksum Eroor) Can U hel me
>, PLEASE ? I remeber this happening before also, The only extenino that I
>have added si the EasyLife 1 , that werks :(

I've had this problem before, I think it may be because there is
an S drawer in your Amos pro drawer. This means that although the
Config editor saves S:AMOSPro_Interpreter_Config Amos actually
reads the file at AMOSPro_System:S/AMOSPro_Interpreter_Config.

The simple way to fix this is to delete the S drawer in you Amospro
folder.

If this is not the case then I'd have no idea what it could be :(


Hope it works now, see ya.

	Message #210 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

columns

Tue Jul 7, 1998 7:09 pm
Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>


Using the highligths program that was sent here earlier
by Bernie Noel <bnoel@club-internet.fr>
I wonder how to print many 'Options' on screen in
columns, something like this:



Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1


I need something like 45 different Options.




The program must be in Hires.
The colour of each option can be the same.



I'd also like to know how to print it like this:

Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1

Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1

Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1
Option 1 Option 1 Option 1




The program is here:




Screen Open 0,640,240,16,Hires
Curs Off : Flash Off : Cls 0

' Initialize text and zones

Reserve Zone 450


Screen Open


FH=8 : Rem font height
XO=12 : YO=8
Ink 6,0

Restore OPTIONS

For I=1 To 450
Read T$
YG=YO+(I-1)*FH
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Set Zone I,XO,YG To XO+Text Length(T$),YG+FH-1
Next


Repeat
Z=Mouse Zone
If Z
YG=YO+(Z-1)*FH
Ink 6,2
Restore OPTIONS
For I=1 To Z : Read T$ : Next
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Repeat
If Mouse Click : Cls
Print "You choosed ";T$ : Exit 2 : End If
Until Mouse Zone<>Z
Ink 6,0
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
End If
Until Mouse Click
'

The program down here prints 45 different texts on screen

-----------------------------------------------------------------

Screen Open 0,640,240,16,Hires
Curs Off : Flash Off : Cls 0

' Initialize text and zones

Reserve Zone 45

FH=8 : Rem font height
XO=12 : YO=8
Ink 6,0
Restore OPTIONS


For I=1 To 25
Read T$
YG=YO+(I-1)*FH

If YG>200 Then Exit : Rem jump to print right column

Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Set Zone I,XO,YG To XO+Text Length(T$),YG+FH-1
Next


XO=320 : YO=8

For I=1 To 20
Read T$
YG=YO+(I-1)*FH

If YG>200 Then Exit : Rem jump to highlite

Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Set Zone I,XO,YG To XO+Text Length(T$),YG+FH-1
Next





Rem Here comes the problem...what must be done to
Rem let highlite and 'mouse click' follow the texts
Rem like they were printed above?





Repeat

Z=Mouse Zone

If Z
YG=YO+(Z-1)*FH
Ink 6,2
Restore OPTIONS
For I=1 To Z : Read T$ : Next
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Repeat
If Mouse Click : Cls
Print "You choosed ";T$ : Exit 2 : End If
Until Mouse Zone<>Z
Ink 6,0
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
End If
Until Mouse Click
'

Cdown



Wait 25 : Clear Key : Wait Key


'

even mailed the List awhile back after I failed in my attempt. Well, I'm at
it again, and I've still got the same problems. I've checked for updates
for all the kickers I used before, and even for new kickers I didn't have.

I did try the existing kicker(s) I have on my A3000 (which I never really
use except for testing). Naturally, it (Softboot) worked as the 3000 was
designed for this very thing, and it functions much like an A1200. However,
my A2000 is a different story. Although it's similar in construction to an
A500, I still can't get any kicker to work with it. My configuration is as:

Amiga 2000, accelerated w/PP&S 68040, 68040 FPU, MMU
1MB Chip, 15MB 32-bit Fast; 105MB Quantum HD, 105MB SyQuest
Internal Commodore IBM-PC/XT Bridgeboard, 2 external floppies
I'm currently running Kickstart 2.04 (37.175) and Workbench 2.1

I have tried the following kickers (all that I can remeber):
SoftKick 3.43 (can't match the kickstarts to relocation tables,
and I get nothing after (force) kicking except flashing bars,
indicating something going on with the MMU and Captures() I think)

MKick 1.09 (works, but needs 1.3 and doesn't survive a hard-reset)
ZKick 1.21 (same as MKick, needs 1.3, but doesn't work as well).

ReKick 1.xx (Giark sent me this the first time around, obviously
for use under 1.3 or an A500/2000, but never would work right.
Wouldn't rekick into new kickstart, and after reboot would lose HD).

Set040 (came with my '040 card, but won't kick 3.0) :|
LKick ?.xx (I've read about it, not very dependable).

PLEASE NOTE: I would NEED/PREFER a kicker that kicks UNDER 2.04+ !

If anyone thinks they can offer any VALUABLE help, please contact me. Also,
if you think you can help but you need more detailed specs, contact me and
I can give you almost anything you need (SysInfo is so handy). This isn't
urgent, but is a problem I will have to solve in the near future. Thnx.

	Message #225 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

random once

Thu Jul 9, 1998 1:37 am
Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>


This program goes to each label randomly
exactly once.

I don't understand why it works...

Maybe someone could try to explain how it works?



Dim USED(10)
Do
_START:
X=Rnd(9)+1
If USED(X)<>0 Then Goto _START
USED(X)=1
Goto(X)
1
Print "1" : Goto _START
2
Print "2" : Goto _START
3
Print "3" : Goto _START
4
Print "1" : Goto _START
5
Print "2" : Goto _START
6
Print "3" : Goto _START
7
Print "1" : Goto _START
8
Print "2" : Goto _START
9
Print "3" : Goto _START
10
Print "1" : Goto _START


Loop

--
----------------------------------------------------------------
 greets  grok@flashback.net  (or: grok@online.idg.se)

	Message #228 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: random once

Wed Jul 8, 1998 9:17 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi, Hakan


Here is how (I think) the program works, line by line :)


>Dim USED(10)
This sets the table up for storing which line you've been to.

>Do
>_START:
>X=Rnd(9)+1
Makes x = a random number 1-10

>If USED(X)<>0 Then Goto _START
Here is where the program checks the table to see if the no.
has been used yet. It works like this:
When you start the program all the entrys in the table are
set to 0, so when it checks entry X, if it hasn't been done
then it carrys on (0<>0 is false). If it has been used already
then the entry is 1 and it Goes to _START (1<>0 is true)

>USED(X)=1
As the no. X hasn't been used yet (or it would goto _start)
the program sets entry X to 1 so the program will never use
that line again.

>Goto(X)
Now it finally goes to line X

>1
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>2
>Print "2" : Goto _START
>3
>Print "3" : Goto _START
>4
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>5
>Print "2" : Goto _START
>6
>Print "3" : Goto _START
>7
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>8
>Print "2" : Goto _START
>9
>Print "3" : Goto _START
>10
>Print "1" : Goto _START


>Loop

There you go, I hope that clears every thing up with you :)


See ya.


--

	Message #229 of 8174

Serial Device Headaches

Tue Jul 7, 1998 8:16 pm
<Declan_Gorman@modusmedia.com>

Greetings,

I am coding a utility to record and playback System Exclusive
messages from midi devices and have run into a problem. My program
pauses until a SysEx message is received at the serial port. With
this it counts the number of messages and calculates the size of the
file being produced.

My problem is that every now and then, AMOSPro V2 reports the error
Hardware Data Overrun. The manual states that this error is generated
if you wait too long before loading your data from the serial port
using Serial Input$. It gives two options to try an overcome this,
use Serial Get(), which I am using or alter the Serial Speed, which I
assume I cannot as Midi data is transmitted at a fixed speed.
Sometimes my program record over 700 messages and other times it may
record 16, it varies.

My program checks for the existence of data at the serial port and
just loops if nothing is there. I have also tried a Serial Check()
but it doesn't seem to work. Can anyone help or give some advice? I
have included the source for the main receiving code below. Thanks in
advance.

Declan.

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Procedure _RECEIVE_BULK

_BYTES=0
_MESSAGES=0
_POINTER=_BYTES : Rem Recording pointer of data in memory
_SYSEX=False : Rem Currently we do not have a sysex message
_BIM=0 : Rem Bytes in message, used to delete incomplete last message

Repeat

SEL=Gui Event

_OVERRUN=Serial Status(0)

If _OVERRUN=8
Gui Reset : Edit
End If

_RECEIVE=Serial Get(0)

If _RECEIVE>-1
If _RECEIVE<128 and _SYSEX=True
Inc _BYTES
Poke Start(10)+_POINTER,_RECEIVE
Inc _POINTER
Inc _BIM

Else

If _RECEIVE=240 : Rem 240=$F0 - Start of Sysex'
Inc _MESSAGES
Inc _BYTES
Poke Start(10)+_POINTER,_RECEIVE
Inc _POINTER
Inc _BIM
_SYSEX=True

Else

If _RECEIVE=247 : Rem 247=$F7 - End of Sysex'
Inc _BYTES
Poke Start(10)+_POINTER,_RECEIVE
Inc _POINTER
Inc _BIM
_SYSEX=False
End If

End If
End If
End If

If _BYTES=_BUFFSIZE Gui Beep
_STOP=True
End If

If SEL=4
_STOP=True
End If

Until _STOP=True

If _SYSEX=True
Dec MESSAGES
_BYTES=_BYTES-_BIM
For N=0 To BIM
Poke Start(10)+_POINTER-1,0
Next N
End If

Serial Close 0 : Gui Reset : Amos To Front : Edit Gui Beep : Wait 50

Bsave "user1.303",Start(10) To Start(10)+Length(10)

_END:
End Proc

MPD Goings on

Wed Jul 8, 1998 8:46 pm
Andy Kellett <mushypd@redrose.net>


Hi everyone. Seeing as I was being asked about and moaned at about the FTP
site, i figured I would explain a bit in detail as to what is currently
going on here at MPD headquarters.

Firstly, im converting my entire Amiga setup to that of an Ethernet. Im
doing this now, for when my other (at least) 4 Amiga machines are finished
building, each will have its own task of running web, FTP, and mailservers
etc. so I figure the practise now is better than panicing later. It works
good too, have it hooked to the PC with a 56K modem, which means lovely FTP
transfer rates.

The FTP server is also being transferred to the PC as I speak. The PC has a
56K modem on it now, and also has much better handling performances when it
comes to multiple users. All FTP services will be down for at least another
week. Those with private FTP accounts, get in touch with me telling me your
usernames and passwords (I cant see what they were in miami!) immediately,
otherwise you will be deleted.

Over the course of the next 6-10 weeks, i will be working extremely heavily
with Blitz 2, converting my mailinglist software to run on this terrible
language. I wanted to keep it completely in AMOS, but unfortunately AMOS
just can't handle everything I want to throw at it, and im having to limit
the software by large extremes just to keep it from GURU'ing all the time.
Ill still be on the list, i have no intentions of deleting the AMOS site,
so no need to panic!!

All AMOSPro compilers have veen sold. Dont ask me for anymore at this time,
i shall let you know when I get some in. Thanks to all those who have
purchased them.

Well, time for me to go. Live long and prosper!

Mush

	Message #233 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: random once

Wed Jul 8, 1998 10:02 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org>


On 08-Jul-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
>I don't understand why it works...
>Maybe someone could try to explain how it works?

The USED array keeps track of which labels have been hit. If it has been, it
won't go to that number again. Pretty simple. Check it out with my additions.

>Dim USED(10)
>Do

COUNT=0

>_START:
>X=Rnd(9)+1
>If USED(X)<>0 Then Goto _START
>USED(X)=1

COUNT=COUNT+1
If COUNT=10 Then Exit

>Goto(X)
>1
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>2
>Print "2" : Goto _START
>3
>Print "3" : Goto _START
>4
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>5
>Print "2" : Goto _START
>6
>Print "3" : Goto _START
>7
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>8
>Print "2" : Goto _START
>9
>Print "3" : Goto _START
>10
>Print "1" : Goto _START
>Loop

Well met and godspeed,

<Declan_Gorman@modusmedia.com>


I have a question about the LDOS extension, in particular the Arexx
support. I am looking to send information to OctaMED Sound Studio
from my program every time a slider is moved or string in entered.
LDos provides a command which goes like this......

A$=Lrexx Send Msg("Host-Name","Message",Result)

For my program I am using......

Host$="octamed_rexx"+chr$(0)
Message$="in_select"+str$(instrument)+chr$(0)

Send_Message$=Lrexx Send Msg(Host$,Message$,0)

Within my program I have checked for the existence of the OctaMED
arexx port but it reports it as not open. I do have OctaMED running
and I know that the port is open.

If I enter a Arexx Open("octamed_rexx") command into my program, it
freezes amos.

What am I doing wrong it regards to addressing the OctaMED arexx Port?

Declan.

> show on a real 3.1 amiga?
>
> Any1 got any ideas?
I`ve seen this bug at work. I saw it when I tried to run a animation
sequence on a PPC and a 68040 both running WB3.1 On the PPC the screen
was visible, but every second line was gone and on the 040 the program
crashed out when trying to display the screen. Getting the new Amos lib
apparently fixes the problem.

Seeya,
Andy H.

	Message #266 of 8174

Re: (no subject) [Doom engine]

Sat Jul 11, 1998 9:21 pm
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


> Has anyone out there wrote a Doom style game engine.I would be suprised
> if there was no-one as AMOS is pretty good for that style. By writing the
> engine I don`t mean using AMOS 3D I mean writing using the polygon
> command and rotating them around a point.

I've had a 3D engine in the works for several months now (I've made several
sets of code to make it fast, more accurate, and work), and although I've
halted the major work of it for now (for the anticipated release of
AMOS_3), I'm working on a new set of coverted code. Hopefully, after I have
a working basic engine, I'll incorporate it into a game (ideas welcome).
Hopefully I can still get some speed out of AMOS Pro yet, with the help of
some Extensions. Anything that comes of it will be posted on Parrottsoft.

(Btw, the engine for now is just your basic Wolfenstein-er/Blake Stone. I
may end up doing either an update or an entirely new engine that is
Doom-like using sectors etc., but realize that a Doomer is harder to code.)

(YES) Soft-kicking problem solved! (YES)

Tue Jul 14, 1998 10:04 pm
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


To those whom it may concern (Yes yes yes yes!):

For some time now, I've been trying (and failing) at soft-kicking OS3.1
onto my A2000 (which is running 2.1). I had tried almost _every_ kicker I
could find on Aminet, but nothing would work. I am now pleased to announce:

I HAD DID IT! I HAVE PULLED IT OFF! I now have 3.1 softbooting on my A2000!
I won't go into details as to how I finally managed to get it to work,
although if you are interested, mail me and I'll send you a breif account
(as this may help anyone else in the future who had the same problems I
did). It ended up working through the combined help of Mkick and sKick.

I would like to go ahead and send some small thanks out to Giark,
Mush, and PAC for the help they offered (the little bit if not much).

Believe it or not, I still have one small problem: My default OS is 2.1 (in
ROM), and so I have a requester pop-up at startup to ask if I want to go
ahead and boot or softkick into 3.1. Either way it's going to automatically
boot off my DH0: partition. I was wondering if perhaps there is a program
that will patch the Kickstart image so I could change the default boot
partition (i.e. DH0: -> DH2:)? I'm basically looking for a way _AROUND_
having to use the 3.1 boot menu (LMB+RMB) at startup, changing it from DH0
to DH2. Any help with this problem would be greatly appreciated. Thanks.

Adam Parrott, mailto: parrotta@usa.net, ICQ# 12967025, Handle: Axianator

	Message #286 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: (YES) Soft-kicking problem solved! (YES)

Tue Jan 3, 1978 4:23 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 15-Jul-98, Adam Parrott wrote:


>To those whom it may concern (Yes yes yes yes!):

Hiya!

>I would like to go ahead and send some small thanks out to Giark,
>Mush, and PAC for the help they offered (the little bit if not much).

>Believe it or not, I still have one small problem: My default OS is 2.1 (in
>ROM), and so I have a requester pop-up at startup to ask if I want to go
>ahead and boot or softkick into 3.1. Either way it's going to automatically
>boot off my DH0: partition. I was wondering if perhaps there is a program
>that will patch the Kickstart image so I could change the default boot
>partition (i.e. DH0: -> DH2:)? I'm basically looking for a way _AROUND_
>having to use the 3.1 boot menu (LMB+RMB) at startup, changing it from DH0
>to DH2. Any help with this problem would be greatly appreciated. Thanks.

There is a MUCH MUCH easier way just..
simply set the partitions priority in HDToolBox, its pretty easy to do, just
set which ever drive you want to boot to priority '1' and all other drives to
have
a LOWER priority(ie. -5,-6,-7etc..). OR you can select them just not to be
bootable
in HDToolBox, this way you cant set there priority, so just Hd2: will boot.

cya,

Iconify

Tue Jan 3, 1978 4:21 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


Hi,

As some of you know TGE will have a Iconify command
(G Iconify ICON$). There are a few diffrent ways of having
the command, which do you think is best:

1. The command will close all screens, stop music free mem
and restore EVERYTHING back when the icon is double clicked on.

2. The command just puts amos to back, frees no mem.

3. The command will Close all screens, stop all music
but the user will have to draw everything that was of the screen
back onto it themself.

4. It will JUST draw the icon on WB, the user will be left to close
everything, and send amos to back.

With No.1 IT wont be able to close windows, GUIs, etc..

Please Pick the one you think is best.

Also seen as Im putting the Iconify in, I could add the ability
to read ToolTypes, or does anyone know if any other extension already does it ?

thanks,

	Message #299 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: buffer size

Sat Jul 18, 1998 3:55 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org>


On 18-Jul-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
>Is there some way to increase the
>default buffer size for program listings?

It's in interpreter config or editor config. If you change it, you need to
turn off autorestore (or whatever it is called) first. Otherwise, it will keep
giving you the 32k buffer, due to the restore. Right now, I use a buffer of
500k for my program space.

Re: Iconify

Sat Jul 18, 1998 7:52 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hello Stacey

On 17-Lug-98, Stacey Abshire wrote: [amos-list] Re: Iconify


>> Hi,
>>
>> As some of you know TGE will have a Iconify command
>> (G Iconify ICON$). There are a few diffrent ways of having
>> the command, which do you think is best:
>>
>> 1. The command will close all screens, stop music free mem
>> and restore EVERYTHING back when the icon is double clicked on.
>>
>> 2. The command just puts amos to back, frees no mem.
>>
>> 3. The command will Close all screens, stop all music
>> but the user will have to draw everything that was of the screen
>> back onto it themself.
>>
>> 4. It will JUST draw the icon on WB, the user will be left to close
>> everything, and send amos to back.


Option 4 is the best because you can safely close everythings... only the
coders know the best method to deallocate their resources, how and when.

So just popup the icon and sen amos to back. The GUI extension will use the
same tecnique.

>> Also seen as Im putting the Iconify in, I could add the ability
>> to read ToolTypes, or does anyone know if any other extension already
>> does it ?

AMCAF

	Message #301 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: GUI game

Sat Jul 18, 1998 7:45 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hello Stephen

On 17-Lug-98, Stephen Lebed wrote: [amos-list] GUI game

> 1) I'm using BOB CLEAR/DRAW to update my double buffer display. When I use
> GUI CLONE, only the power meter is updated on the P96 screen (the power
> meter is drawn on the lowres display). All the bobs are not copied. I
> thought GUI CLONE would do a screen grab of the lowres display and copy it
> to the P96?

GUI Clone doesn't copy your screen datas, but allows the intuition screen to
display the Amos bitmaps. The Bob Clear/Draw command doesn't work correclty
because your Amos screen is double buffered, and Gui Clone cannot handle
double buffered display.


> 2) Will it be possible to create a double buffered screen?

No.

> 3) How can I create graphics for a game using 256 color or more? Will the
> GET BOB command grab more than 5 bitplanes?

No.

> 4) Is there a bug in the GUI iff display command? In the example program
> the image in the bank will only displat on a PAL screen. I can't get it to
> redisplay to anything else.

Actually the GUI Display Iff command display the picture using the monitor ID
specified on the IFF file only. You can't display it in a different screen
mode...



--


Bye!

	Message #305 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Modems in Amos

Mon Jul 20, 1998 12:27 pm
"Cox, Michael D" <michael.cox@eds.com>


> Does anyone know how to use a modem in amos? I've tried
sending
>the string 'AT&F1&D2\r' and then 'ATDT*****' but this just
returns
>the string straight back.
I think it is supposed to send it back. I think the modem's defaults
are to echo back what you type. Probably what you need to do is do an
ATZ\r then loop waiting for the data "OK". If it does not receive OK
then maybe you have result codes turned off?

	Message #310 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: I/O Errors

Mon Jul 20, 1998 3:35 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org>


On 20-Jul-98, Andy H wrote:
> Load "<mysoundbank>",5
>The first time around it works fine. Then the next time or maybe 3rd or
>4th time around it crashes with an "I/O Error".

Are you using Erase All at the start of your program? You know that amos does
not erase banks on its own. You may be filling up your chip mem with instances
of the bank, then, once chip is full, you can't load anymore. If you don't
want all banks cleared before you get into the program, try using Erase 5.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark

                                       giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org

	Message #311 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: I/O Errors

Mon Jul 20, 1998 4:19 pm
"Scooter D. Matott sXe" <sdmatott@midway.uchicago.edu>


> On 20-Jul-98, Andy H wrote:
> > Load "<mysoundbank>",5
> >The first time around it works fine. Then the next time or maybe 3rd or
> >4th time around it crashes with an "I/O Error".
>
> Are you using Erase All at the start of your program? You know that amos does
> not erase banks on its own. You may be filling up your chip mem with instances
> of the bank, then, once chip is full, you can't load anymore.

Could this also be the nefarious Amiga memory fragmentation curse?
If you keep loading different size songs then your Amiga's ram gets all
chopped up to pieces and eventually no matter what you do or how much ram
you have free you can't load a file because there isn't enough contiguous
ram left. The only solution is to reboot so you could be in bigger
trouble than Giark suggests, how big are the songs your loading, reloading
a few 1-200k files might be ok but if your files are more on the order
of 4-500+ kilobytes long your headed for trouble.
                Scott Matott sXe

Re: Apps for Writing AmigaGuide Documentation and Installer scripts?

Mon Jul 20, 1998 5:00 pm
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


> From: "Cox, Michael D" <michael.cox@eds.com>

> I was wondering, what (if any) application is out there that could help
> me write the AmigaGuide documentation for my CD Player? I really want
> something easy that I do not have to know AmigaGuide codes or anything.

I would _HIGHLY_ recommend Heddley (by Ed Dumbill). You can find it under
text/hyper on Aminet. The latest version is 1.1 (Heddley11.lha). I have yet
to make a full Amigaguide doc with it, but it has many a feature and looks
EXTREMELY cool. It's also the only one I could find on Aminet :)

> is there the same type of application for writing an Installer script?

The only one I've found on Aminet is called ScriptMaker. The filename is
"ScriptMaker20.lha" and is under util/misc. I haven't tried it yet, but it
looks like the only Install-script generator there is on Aminet.

Re: Modems in Amos-fixed

Tue Jul 21, 1998 12:05 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


On 20-Jul-98, Cox, Michael D wrote:
>From: "Cox, Michael D" <michael.cox@eds.com>

>> Does anyone know how to use a modem in amos? I've tried
>sending
>>the string 'AT&F1&D2\r' and then 'ATDT*****' but this just
>returns
>>the string straight back.
>I think it is supposed to send it back. I think the modem's defaults
>are to echo back what you type. Probably what you need to do is do an
>ATZ\r then loop waiting for the data "OK". If it does not receive OK
>then maybe you have result codes turned off?

Ok I've found out why it didn't work, you have to send
"ATZ\r"+Chr$(13)+Chr$(10), now I'll be able to add modem commands
to some of my games :)

	Message #325 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: I/O Errors

Tue Jul 21, 1998 3:50 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org>


On 20-Jul-98, Andy H wrote:
>If I want to load the sound in should I erase the bank if it exists?

I always use Erase All at the start of my programs. It keeps the memory frag
problem from cropping up.

>What I have been doing in the past is just loading the next file into
>the bank completely destroying the old one. Which process fragments
>memory quicker?

That's what does it. Amos doesn't really load on top of the old one, it sort
of grabs a new memory hunk.

If you're just testing the program and running it a lot, try doing the load
command the first time you run it, then commenting it out and let amos hold
the sound bank in ram for you.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark

	Message #333 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: More colorful Bobs?

Wed Jul 22, 1998 9:12 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


On 21-Jul-98, Stephen Lebed wrote:
>From: "Stephen Lebed" <slebed@ix.netcom.com>


>Is there a way to create bobs with more than 32 colors?

>Could it be done with paste bob?

>Thanks
>Stephen Lebed


64 colour EHB bobs are no problem. If you wait for a good AGA extention
then that should offer 256 colour bobs.

IF you cant wait for that then 4096 colour HAM6 bobs will work, but
you have to understand how HAM works otherwise the bobs & backgrounds
probably won't display properly.

Don't forget that the more colours you use the slower the bobs will
be, so insted of having more colours using a better palette can
make bobs look more colourful.



--

Re: Printer Dump

Fri Jul 24, 1998 3:28 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org>


On 24-Jul-98, Nikola Smolenski wrote:
>I have no FM, I think I've lost it when i was moving... However, any number
>I try simply crashes system after printing.

Value Name Description
$0001 MILCOLS px is in 1/1000"
$0002 MILROWS py is in 1/1000"
$0004 FULCOLS use maximum print width
$0008 FULROWS use maximum print height
$0010 FRACCOLS px is a fraction of FULCOLS
$0020 FRACROWS py is a fraction of FULROWS
$0040 CENTRE centre the image on the page
$0080 ASPECT retain the original aspect ratio
$0100 DENSITY1 low density
$0200 DENSITY2
$0300 DENSITY3
$0400 DENSITY4
$0500 DENSITY5
$0600 DENSITY6
$0700 DENSITY7
$0800 NOFORMFEED do not eject paper
$1000 TRUSTME do not reset
$2000 NOPRINT donot print

	Message #352 of 8174

Re: (Off Topic) Hard Drive problems

Fri Jul 24, 1998 4:01 pm
"Stephen Lebed" <slebed@ix.netcom.com>


As soon as possible you should get all your important data off the drive.
The startup-slow down is the motor controller dying. I've had this problems
countless times. In a very short time the whole drive will not be
accessable.

Stephen Lebed

	Message #354 of 8174

Re: (Off Topic) Hard Drive problems

Fri Jul 24, 1998 4:49 pm
"Stephen Lebed" <slebed@ix.netcom.com>


There is no way to replace the motor. Hard drives are built to such an
exacting standard that its just not possible.

I had asked all these same questions. I contacted a company that does data
retrieval, they are the best in the US. They wanted $3000US to TRY to get
the data off. They don't guarantee they can do it.

	Message #355 of 8174: ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Printer Dump

Fri Jul 24, 1998 7:21 pm
Jens Vang Petersen <top_cat@post8.tele.dk>


Hello Nikola

On 23-Jul-98, Nikola Smolenski smashed the keyboard with:
> From: Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>
>
> C'mon, guys! It's impossible that noone of you know this!
>
> I need help about Printer Dump command. Help says that there is a possible
> usage: Printer Dump x1,x2 to y1,y2,px,py,s . s is a special command
> parameter which tells printer precisely how to draw an image to the paper.
> Could someone give me the list of possible values for s and their effect?

I saw that someone else have typed the values up, so I won't, but it should
be noted that the original IO-Devices extension for AMOS Pro holds a
stack-handeling error when using the full syntax resulting in a crash.
I made a fixed version some time ago and mailed it to the list, it can also
be found on my homepages at:

'http://home8.inet.tele.dk/top_cat/'

Please note that the printer.device is very sensitive, so if you send
parameters to it that don't make sense it crashes before printing,
the AMOS command holds NO checking for values.... It's possible
to ask the device to dump a screen as a size of 0*0 dots, crash...

--

	Message #365 of 8174 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: ham mode?

Sun Jul 26, 1998 10:46 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


On 26-Jul-98, Skid wrote:
>From: Skid <skid@angelic.com>

>Heyas again!

>It took me a while to find this new list.
>I've been away from the list since it went to the new addy.
>Can anyone inform me of the status of Amos 3?
>Also, for amos pro 2, What exactly can I do using the HAM mode?
>Are there any restrictions?


Here are the easiest things to do with HAM:

* 4096 colour static screens (title screen pic. etc)

* 4096 colour backgrounds with sprites (only scroll a ham screen
up or down or they'll look weird)

* 4096 colour bobs on a 16 colour bg. (make sure you give the bobs
an outline with one of the first 16 colours)

* Horizontal colour fades like in the Hired Guns title screen.


There is probably more you could do with HAM, but thats what I'd use
them for.


See ya.

--

	Message #374 of 8174

Re: ham is hell!

Mon Jul 27, 1998 9:05 pm
Stacey Abshire <sabshire@kanawhascales.com>


the palette has to be set right. For AMOS, 64 color mode is EHB or
extra half-bright, which means that the second 64 colors are just half
as bright as the first 32 colors. You can't set the values of the last
32 directly. So, that is your problem. You need to make them 32
colors., or figure out a way to set the colors in the last 32 registers
to half as bright from under Photoshop.

	Message #375 of 8174

Re: ham is hell!

Mon Jul 27, 1998 9:46 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> I'm making a game on the PC ( I know, kill me ),

I wish people would quit apologizing for their PC development!!
What's important is that you are doing SOMETHING (of course, it's
always nice when the Amiga benefits from your work). :-)


> anyway, I'm also trying to make it on the miggy at the same time with
> AMOS. Now, I use photoshop for my graphics on the PC, then I save them
> as IFF and reduce the palette to 64 colors for AMOS.. well, it appears
> AMOS doesn't like Dpaint 4 or something.. my colors get all screwed up.
> Is there a way to get this to stop? Or is it only possible to use Dpaint3
> drawn stuff in AMOS?

You didn't mention exactly where in the conversion process you are
using Dpaint 4 and what you are doing with it...

I convert images over from my PC quite often and would use this
sequence for your conversion:

You need some Amiga tool capable of creating HAM images in order
to convert the 64-color image to an Amiga HAM image... try
something like the old HamLab if you can find it. I think I have it on
my harddrive someplace...
--- OR ---
You could simply try using 64 colour EHB mode which is much easier
to find support for (most popular Amiga Paint software supports EHB).

Assuming you're going with EHB...

1. Transfer the 64-color image to DPaint.

2. Convert the image to a 64-colour (32+32 in reality) EHB image.

3. Save this image and all should be well.

However, I have sometimes noticed that Amiga paint programs save
the palette in rgb8 (AGA) instead of rgb4 (OCS/ECS) which AMOS cannot
handle.

To get around this problem, simply boot your Amiga into OCS/ECS
mode using the Early Startup Menu(?) and then your paint software
will save the palette info in the correct format.

Hope this helps, if not e-mail me the image and I'll have a go at
converting it for you.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

Re: ham is hell!

Tue Jul 28, 1998 12:12 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

On 27-Jul-98, Garfield Benjamin wrote:
> From: "Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>

>> I'm making a game on the PC ( I know, kill me ),

> I wish people would quit apologizing for their PC development!!
> What's important is that you are doing SOMETHING (of course, it's
> always nice when the Amiga benefits from your work). :-)

Theres nothing wrong with writing PC programs, unless you wear glasses,
have a stupidly large grin, make far too much money and go by the name
of '/Bill/' (I need not say any more)

>> anyway, I'm also trying to make it on the miggy at the same time with
>> AMOS. Now, I use photoshop for my graphics on the PC, then I save them
>> as IFF and reduce the palette to 64 colors for AMOS.. well, it appears
>> AMOS doesn't like Dpaint 4 or something.. my colors get all screwed up.
>> Is there a way to get this to stop? Or is it only possible to use Dpaint3
>> drawn stuff in AMOS?

Is that DPaint 4 AGA, if it is then Garfield is right, dont set the
screenmode at 64 colours, simply put it to EHB mode .
AMOS Screwed the 64 Colour pics up because it sees 64 colours as EHB,
when in your case I guess it isn't. If the worst comes to the worst then
just make do with 32 colours (AMOS will work faster with less colours)

If you just want the gfx as static screens then why not use HAM6,
DPaint4 and Amos are quite happy to use that mode.

(I'd use something like ImageFX for converting images, it was free on
an AF disk, I could send you a copy if you want ;)


> However, I have sometimes noticed that Amiga paint programs save
> the palette in rgb8 (AGA) instead of rgb4 (OCS/ECS) which AMOS cannot
> handle.

Thats really not a problem as amos seems to automatically reduce the
palette, so although you dont get all the shades, it should still look
alright. (At least with DPaint V+ImageFX)


See ya.
--

CBATNAM

Tue Jul 28, 1998 4:05 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


Cap'n Bubba
And The
Nasty Alien Menace

Intro
Orbiting above the planet Earth, the
AMOS (Atmospheric Monitoring Orbital
Station) circles in its steady path.

Aboard the AMOS, Cap'n Bubba, aging
superhero, was relaxing in the station
bar (Actually, he was hiding from the
Tax Man, but he's supposed to be a
hero, so forget I ever said anything.)
when an urgent message came in over the
HeroPhone. (Actually, he saw it written
on the men's room wall, but that doesn't
sound nearly so heroic, so, again,
forget I said anything.)

Before Stage 1

There was no time to waste, and no time
to call for reinforcements. Cap'n
Bubba grabbed his trusty Jet-Pac (Er,
actually a couple of fire extinguishers
duct taped together.) and headed off
into the stratosphere to fight the Nasty
Alien Menace (who aren't really nasty at
all, or even all that menacing, but
every hero needs someone to beat the tar
out of, and they lost the toss).

Play Stage 1

Before Stage 2

Cap'n Bubba hurtled through the
atmosphere of the Nasty Alien Planet,
propelled by his Jet-Pac, shooting his
trusty Violence-Dealing Shooter (Okay,
his bubble gun. You're not getting into
the spirit of this hero idea, are you?)
and flew off in search of the Nasty
Alien Menace's main base (or the nearest
bar, whichever came first).

Play Stage 2

Before Stage 3

Cap'n Bubba dropped his VDS (He was out
of bubble juice.) and shed his Jet-Pac
(No more CO2 either.) and strapped on
his dueling gloves to face the Nasty
Alien Guards (or old ladies, or pet
hamsters or anything. It'd been quite
some time since Cap'n Bubba had a drink
and he was getting a bit testy. Well,
how would YOU feel if you were in his
place?) that stood between him and the
Dungeon Of Ultimate Terror (which,
rumour has it, is one hell of a fine
bar, as well as being home to some of
the sweetest exotic dancers in the
galaxy).

Play Stage 3

Before Stage 4

Having defeated the guards (Cap'n Bubba
is something of a dirty fighter, you
see), Cap'n Bubba entered the Dungeon Of
Ultimate Terror (which, it turns out, is
NOT one hell of a fine bar and is
inhabited by Nasty Aliens, not exotic
dancers).

Play Stage 4

Before Bonus Stage

Oh, No! Cap'n Bubba is hallucinating
again (Too much drinking). The good news
is that he could pick up some nifty
bonuses if he can concentrate. The bad
news is that the hallucinations won't
last very long.

Win

The struggle is over. Cap'n Bubba has
defeated the Nasty Alien Menace (through
trickery and dirty pool) and swiped
enough treasure to pay off the Tax Man.
The only bad news is that there is not a
bar in sight!

Lose

The struggle is over. Cap'n Bubba, once
a mighty superhero, is now nothing but a
pathetic drunk. To make matters worse,
the Tax Man is dating Cap'n Bubba's
former girlfriend.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark
                                             ICQ 12235820
                                       giark@hicksville.dyn.ml.org
                                http://www.hicksville.dyn.ml.org/~giark/
                            .----------------------------------------------.
                            |      ______  ______    _____                 |
                            |     / ____/ / __  /   / ___ \ Makers of      |
                            |    / /__   / /_/ /   / /  / / SoloTrek II    |
                            |   / ___/  / ____ \  / /  / /                 |
                            |  / /     / /___/ / / /  / /   CyberSpace BBS |
                            | /_/     /_______/ /_/  /_/    (519)579-0072  |

Yep, I think once you change the partition sizes you loos everthing
on those partitions (I guess you'd have to shrink a different parition
first).

Before you did any partition work you'd have to backup all your
partitions you are re-sizing. Of course if you dont want that
hassle you could use something like DiskExpander to compress you HD.
(It would make it slower though).

Re: (Off Topic) Hard Drive problems

Tue Jul 28, 1998 2:55 am
Andy Gibson <andy@agasinc.demon.co.uk>


This message arrived in my mail box:
Date: Friday 24-Jul-98
Time: 15:01:37
Name: Stephen Lebed
Subject: [amos-list] Re: (Off Topic) Hard Drive problems
So here's a reply...

Hi there,


>As soon as possible you should get all your important data off the drive.
>The startup-slow down is the motor controller dying. I've had this problems
>countless times. In a very short time the whole drive will not be
>accessable.
>Stephen Lebed

That's sound advice, and you may want to take Stephen up on that. It's
ALWAYS advisable to back up important data anyway, just in case...

(I'm sure we have all lost some important stuff due to o backup!)

Anyway, my previous email on this subject stated I had a similar
problem a while ago with a HD and a new PSU sorted it out.

That HD is still going strong (in another A1200), but re-reading your
(Declan's) original email, it may be that Stephen is correct in
stating that you HD is about to die :(

So, go on, back up important stuff NOW. Then get hold of a PSU and see
how you get on. If that doesn't work, get a new HD and be thankful you
got the data backed up in the nick of time, and, err...thank Stephen
too :-)

	Message #394 of 8174

Re: Re partitioning Workbench

Wed Jul 29, 1998 1:02 am
Richard Griffith <ragriffi@sprynet.com>


On 28-Jul-98, Rod Whiteley wrote:

>I was just about to increase the size of my Workbench partition via
>HDToolbox
>(since I'm forever deleting stuff when installing software, fonts etc.)
>when I
>vaguely recalled something about re-partitioning resulting in vast
>amounts of
>lost data on original partitions.

Only ALL of it is lost. Backup all the data in all partitions you will
change. Repartitioning will make it ALL inaccessible. To be safe, you
should backup everything on the drive, as it is very easy to make a
mistake, and very painful to recover, if you don't lose it forever.
At the very least, make detailed notes about the start and stop
cyliders for each existing partition. Even a change by one cylinder
will render a partition useless.

I've changed things many times, but I once spent 5 hours locating
the partitions on a small drive for a friend of mine, who had been
trying to setup a zip drive, and managed to scramble his harddrive.

> Can I increase the partition size without tears via HDToolBox?

As long as you take reasonable precautions and know what you are
doing, it is fairly easy. If in doubt, get help.

-Richard

	Message #397 of 8174

Various Questions & more......

Wed Jul 29, 1998 12:07 pm
"Declan Gorman" <declan_gorman@modusmedia.com>


When I was finished writing, I realised how long it was so my apologies if
the size of this email upsets anyone.

I thought I would share with you guys, some info on my current AMOS Pro
project......Midi Companion. It is being coded on my 4MB A500+ with Amos
Pro V2 and it makes heavy use of the GUI extension. It is a very useful
utility for users of OctaMED and any Midi equipment, especially the Roland
MC-303 Groovebox. If you have ever used OctaMED you will know that a lot of
"programming" has to be done to access some of the various midi controllers
etc. by using player commands etc. Midi Companion replaces all of this and
much more, giving the user the ability to easily change Bank Select, Midi
Presets, Instrument Pan, Portamento, Effects, Effect Levels, User Definable
NRPNs & the list is continually growing as I update the code.

At the moment V1.6r is the latest evaluation release and is available for
download from http://members.tripod.com/~Declan/midi_com.htm and V1.7r will
be available soon with even more features.

The future?
I hope to integrate full Arexx support within Midi Companion for better
communication with OctaMED and hopefully lead to real-time editing from Midi
Companion sliders into OctaMED tracks.

Bearing in mind this is my first release and first shareware release, I have
a couple of questions regarding the above......

In the evaluation program I have disabled a lot of the extra features, ie.
User Definable NRPNs, Effect Parameters, Load and Save.
Is this a good idea?
I am constantly debating with myself whether I should enable Load & Save in
the hope that people will see more of Midi Companions potential.

The shareware fee I am requesting is £10 Irish punts which is the equivalent
to £8.50 sterling and $14 US dollars. Does this seem to much? Too little?
Just about right?

How can I truly copyright my program?
I don't think that writing (c) Declan Gorman is good enough, or is it?

As far as I know there is no other utility like this for OctaMED and my fear
is that with the release of OctaMED V2 next year, the authors may include a
similar thing within OctaMED itself. Although everything in my program is
based on standard midi controllers and Roland MC-303 specific functions
would I have any legal rights should OctaMED V2 contain similar things?

Am I over reacting? (After all I have already spent 7 months in total on
this project and will continue to develop it as far as I can.)

A short question on hacking......
At present OctaMED does not allow the serial port to be shared (throwing the
concept of multitasking out the window) and I have to have OctaMED Midi
disabled to allow Midi Companion to work and vice versa. Would it be
possible to hack OctaMED and remove the code that prevents multitasking?

Can someone do it for me? (he he)

Any answers or advice on the above would be greatly appreciated.

Declan.

	Message #405 of 8175

Re: Re partitioning Workbench

(Date unavailable)
"David Smith" <dsmith@bexley.u-net.com>


Hello Rod you said:

> I was just about to increase the size of my Workbench partition via HDToolbox
> (since I'm forever deleting stuff when installing software, fonts etc.) when
> I vaguely recalled something about re-partitioning resulting in vast amounts
> of lost data on original partitions. I RTFM, but it just tells me to 'see the
> Amiga hard drive user's guide' where/whatever the hell that is. Can I
> increase the partition size without tears via HDToolBox? Rod

It can be done BUT first back up EVERYTHING on the hard drive. Only when you
are confident you have perfect backups use HDToolbox to re-partition the
drive. After re-partitioning you have to format each changed partition; this
can be a quick-format but without backups you will still need to use DiscSalv
or some such to recover lost files. I speak from experience on this! HDToolbox
issues warnings about what you are doing - read them.

David Smith

	Message #416 of 8175

Re: Semi-non AMOS: C ports

Thu Jul 30, 1998 3:23 am
Richard Griffith <ragriffi@sprynet.com>


On 29-Jul-98, Cox, Michael D wrote:
>From: "Cox, Michael D" <michael.cox@eds.com>

>I was wondering. On the Amiga, when you see a C program and it defines
>a variable to be an integer, how many bytes does that use? I have seen
>2 or 4. Same goes for unsigned integers (2 or 4 bytes). I ask because
>I am writing a program that uses library calls and returns an address
>where a data structure was created. I then read the right number of
>bytes to get the correct info. Let me know if that does not make
sense.

Makes great sense, but the answer may not. Current Amiga C compilers
use 4 byte ints, and some, such as the SAS/LATTICE line always have.
It is usually an option though to switch the default to 2 byte, and
that was the standard for older Manx/Aztec 3.? and below. In general,
code newer than OS2.0 will use long (4 byte) int, but older code may
vary. The best 'C' technique is to use an explicit typedef's for
anything where it really matters (LONG,SHORT,ULONG,USHORT,etc. as the
OS includes provide, and depend on, these) just to eliminate any
confusion. I guess the best answer would be assume long (4 byte size)
unless proven otherwise. For every compiler I can think of, the size
of an int and an unsigned int would be the same by default.

Hope this helps,
-Richard

	Message #418 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Semi-non AMOS: C ports

Thu Jul 30, 1998 10:37 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 29-Jul-98, Cox, Michael D wrote:

CD> I was wondering. On the Amiga, when you see a C program and it defines
CD> a variable to be an integer, how many bytes does that use? I have seen

It depends on a compiler. SAS, for instance, has option SHORTINTEGERS , and
uses 4 bytes without it, and 2 bytes with it.

CD> 2 or 4. Same goes for unsigned integers (2 or 4 bytes). I ask because

They should be same as signed.

CD> I am writing a program that uses library calls and returns an address
CD> where a data structure was created. I then read the right number of
CD> bytes to get the correct info. Let me know if that does not make
sense.

If you want to be sure about size of your data, use WORD or LONG instead of
int . Or you can check data size with sizeof() function.

Note that, in structures, variables are padded to even adresses. So, if you
have

struct somestruct {
char a;
LONG b;
};

it has length of 6, not 5 because there is pad byte between a and b which
is used to store b at even adress.

Regards

	Message #419 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

The AMOS Future

Thu Jul 30, 1998 10:56 am
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hi!

As mentioned in the message subject, i'm here to explain the future and the
present of AMOS.


* PLEASE READ CAREFULLY _ALL _THE MESSAGE!!*


As you know some months ago i've obtained the AMOS sources... in this months
i've spent my time learning the AMOS internal functions and structures,
in order to upgrade it and develop the new AMOSPro V3... but i've to say that
my projects are deeply changed during this period. My original idea was to
upgrade/expand it, add the AGA support and mainly makes it more OS friendly!
but when i've examined the sources some problems are emersed.

Its old AmigsOS v1.3 structure, the total not OS friendly design, and the
confused
programming style, makes it really hard to upgrade as we want.... in order to
obtain the wanted results we have to rewrite it! :'(

So after some meetings with the other developers, we've decided to follow a
bit different way.... probably the /best/ choice for you and for us.


* _AMOS will have a future and also a good present _*




*- The Present -*


We'll release a upgrade package for AMOSPro... you'll obtain:

- expanded/bug fixed version of AMOSPro and compiler
- new extensions
- new tools
- developer infos
- tons of AMOS materials

in detail:

*- EXPANDED BUG FIXED VERSION OF AMOSPRO AND COMPILER*

Self explaning.... we'll try to fix as many bugs as possible, and expand some
Amos functions. In particular i'm working on the AMOS Equates system... the
equate system is a very good idea, but badly implemented. It'll works in a
totally different way, similar to the other languages. I've changed the amos
command Include"".... now it doesn't import a amos source in your program (...
a very stupid idea IMHO in a basic enviroment) but import your symbols. What
symbols? A good news... thanks to the collaboration with Wouter Van
Oortmerssen ( the Amiga E author) Amos will be able to import and use the
Amiga E modules! (supplied with the upgrade or available on Aminet)

The Struct() command has been extended, and now accept a C-like access method

i.e A=Struct(S,"RastPort,BitMap") : Struct(S,"Window,UserData")=255

in the first example you define the variable S as a pointer to a RastPort
structure and then the BitMap field will be returned. In the second S is a ptr
to a Window, and the UserData field will be set to 255.


*- NEW EXTENSIONS*


Since seriously upgrade the main AMOS code isn't possible (... upgrade it
means totally rewrite it!) we've decided to expand it trough our extensions.

This extesions will be added:

- Game Extension
- OsDevKit Extension
- AMCAF Extension
- GUI Extension
- FD Extension
- Turbo Plus 2.15 Registered
- PowerBob 1.1 Registered
- Amos3D *(not confirmed)*



A tipical question.... i already have the GUI Extension, AMCAF etc.. then i
already have the new Amos?????

_/*NO!!!!!*/_

This extensions will be powered! and new functions will be added. Thanks to
the AMOS sources the new extensions will be better and faster.

The /GUI Extension v2.0/ will offers locale support, eXtra Fast Animation
(XFA) format support, a better IFF support, drag'n'drop, app icons, new
advanced internet functions and lot more!


Together the /OsDevKit/ (now its size is greater than the main AMOSPro Lib!)
you'll have the most advanced AmigaOS support available. It supports all the
programming stuff like datatypes, RTG, boopsi, locale, gadtools, intutition
,gfx cards, etc.

The new /FD Extension v3.0/ creates a better code, and as you know it allows
you to integrate as standard Amos commands the functions of all the standard
Amiga libraries (MUI, Exec, Dos etc) using in-line code ie:

A=Lvo MakeVPort(W,V) : A=Lvo Mrgcop(W)


/AMCAF../ well.. probably the most famous Amos extension :) What can i say...
new version = new power!


The /Game/ Extension is the games coders dream.. it allows you to create your
game with AGA support (screens,bobs,gfx...) with a incredible speed!
The Bobs are *4 time faster* than the Amos one! and the most important detail
is the *totally OS friendly design!* plus you'll have a complete CDDA support
and may other useful functions.


_Plus the latest registered versions of Turbo Plus (v2.15) and PowerBobs
(v1.1)._


I'm working on AMOS3D.... i hope to include it in the upgrade release. This
extensions offers a complete access to *ALL* the system resources,
and cover all the programming requirements.

Briefly you'll obtain:

- the complete package AMOSPro + Compiler
- 100% complete AmigaOS support thanks to GUI and OsDevKit
- new Games coding engine... it's AGA, It's fast, it's OS Friendly, it's
easy...
- lots of bug fixes
- cool demos and materials
- our support!! Now you've someone to blame directly if there is something
unstable! :)


*- NEW TOOLS*

Some new tools will be added to the default Amos distribution, for example:


/IED - The Intuition Editor/

This program allows you to use the AMOSPro editor with a intuition screen! Now
you can program in Amos in the WB enviroment... is fantastic drag the AMOS
editor screen together the others ;)


/AmilED - The AMOSPro Interface Language Editor/

It allows you to easly create your interfaces (and sources) in few minutes.
You can directly edit them or create the interfaces using the mouse
(GadToolsBox like), so the source code will be automatically created for you!
Thanks to this function you can create your interfaces without any knowledge
of the Amos interface language!!


/GUI Converter and GTBoxConverter/

This tools allows you to easly import your GadToolsBox GUI in your AMOS
programs as GUI bank or Amos (OsDevKit) source code!


bug fixed version of the standard AMOSPro tools like the Compiler Shell or the
AMAL editor.



/*DEVELOPER INFOS*/

The new AMOSPRO v2.x developer kit will be included, with all the extra tools
never released in the old versions.


*TONS OF AMOS MATERIALS*

Examples,demos,games,sources,extensions, tons of materials coming from the
Mushroom PD library (the new official AMOS library) will be included.



All this stuffs will be released on a CD... the *Amos Developer CD*. The
release date is December '98. The price... not decided yet, /but it'll be very
cheap!/




* _The Future*_


Well... due to the recent Amiga Inc annoncement, the PPC development, the new
top secret CPU and OS is clear that Amos needs to be heavly upgraded to follow
and support the new upcoming standards. But since upgrade AMOS isn't possible
since *its code isn't portable to different CPU*, we've decided to develop a
*NEW LANGUAGE!* Totally written in pure C++, it'll be easly portable on the
different CPUs like 68k and PPC. It's totally OS friendly, and the compiler
can optmize your code! The project name is AMOS NG. Now it's under development
together the AmosPro upgrade... more infos about this project will follow in
the future.


Bye!


                                     !!!

you don't need to specify the bank when loading icons,

"Scooter D. Matott sXe" <sdmatott@midway.uchicago.edu>


> > On the other hand, CDrom drives are VERY cheap today, every one who have an
> > Amiga should buy one and get the complete collection of AMOSUpgrade :).
> >
> > I think, even a poor studen could affort to buy a CDrom drive.
As a poor student myself I can verify this, but the trouble isn't
with getting a cheap CD-Rom it's with getting a decent IDE/SCSI device
cheap. I'm in luck cause my 'miggy is a 3000 with built in SCSI but I
think there are alot of folks on the list with A500 and A1200's who might
not be so lucky, I don't know maybe you guys should speak up!


> I would really dislike future amos command lending atmosphere from C/++.

I for one would love this, give us C-like data structures and
variables whose bit depth can be defined by the coder. Oh but don't lose
one thing, be sure the editor will still 'hide' sub routines ala the
original Amos editor, you would not believe how handy this, or difficult
navigating code can be without it!

        Just my two cents,
                Scott Matott sXe
